## Chapter: Cyberpolitics in International Relations: Theory, Methods, Policy

### Introduction

In today's interconnected world, the use of technology has become an integral part of international relations. The rise of cyberpolitics has brought about new challenges and opportunities for states, organizations, and individuals. This chapter will focus on the comparative analysis and cases in context of cyberpolitics in international relations. 

The first section of this chapter will provide an overview of the theoretical frameworks used to understand cyberpolitics. This will include discussions on the realist, liberal, and constructivist perspectives and how they apply to the realm of cyberpolitics. Additionally, the chapter will explore the role of power, norms, and identity in shaping cyberpolitics.

The second section will delve into the methods used to study cyberpolitics in international relations. This will include an examination of qualitative and quantitative research methods, as well as the challenges and limitations of studying cyberpolitics. The chapter will also discuss the importance of interdisciplinary approaches in understanding this complex and ever-evolving field.

The final section of this chapter will focus on the policy implications of cyberpolitics in international relations. This will include case studies of cyber attacks, cyber espionage, and cyber warfare, and how they have impacted global politics. The chapter will also discuss the role of international organizations and agreements in regulating cyber activities and promoting cyber security.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of cyberpolitics in international relations. By examining theoretical frameworks, research methods, and policy implications, readers will gain a deeper insight into the complexities of this emerging field and its impact on global politics. 


## Chapter: Cyberpolitics in International Relations: Theory, Methods, Policy

### Introduction

In today's interconnected world, the use of technology has become an integral part of international relations. The rise of cyberpolitics has brought about new challenges and opportunities for states, organizations, and individuals. This chapter will focus on the comparative analysis and cases in context of cyberpolitics in international relations. 

The first section of this chapter will provide an overview of the theoretical frameworks used to understand cyberpolitics. This will include discussions on the realist, liberal, and constructivist perspectives and how they apply to the realm of cyberpolitics. Additionally, the chapter will explore the role of power, norms, and identity in shaping cyberpolitics.

### Section 1: Theoretical Frameworks of Cyberpolitics

Theoretical frameworks are essential in understanding the complex and ever-evolving field of cyberpolitics. The realist perspective, which emphasizes the role of power and self-interest in international relations, can be applied to cyberpolitics by examining how states use cyber capabilities to gain advantage over others. This can include cyber espionage, cyber attacks, and cyber warfare. The liberal perspective, on the other hand, focuses on the role of institutions and cooperation in international relations. In the context of cyberpolitics, this can include the role of international organizations and agreements in regulating cyber activities and promoting cyber security. Finally, the constructivist perspective emphasizes the role of norms and identity in shaping international relations. In the realm of cyberpolitics, this can include the development of norms and values surrounding cyber activities, as well as the impact of cyber capabilities on a state's identity and perception in the international community.

### Section 2: Methods of Studying Cyberpolitics

The study of cyberpolitics requires a multidisciplinary approach, as it encompasses various fields such as international relations, computer science, and law. This section will explore the different methods used to study cyberpolitics, including qualitative and quantitative research methods. Qualitative methods, such as case studies and interviews, can provide in-depth insights into specific cyber events and their impact on international relations. Quantitative methods, such as statistical analysis, can help identify patterns and trends in cyber activities. However, studying cyberpolitics also presents unique challenges, such as the difficulty in obtaining accurate and reliable data, as well as the rapid pace of technological advancements. Therefore, interdisciplinary approaches are crucial in gaining a comprehensive understanding of cyberpolitics.

### Section 3: Policy Implications of Cyberpolitics

The final section of this chapter will focus on the policy implications of cyberpolitics in international relations. This will include case studies of cyber attacks, cyber espionage, and cyber warfare, and how they have impacted global politics. The chapter will also discuss the role of international organizations and agreements in regulating cyber activities and promoting cyber security. For instance, the Global Commission on Internet Governance, launched in 2014, has made recommendations about the future of global internet governance and facilitated effective cooperation between relevant international actors. Additionally, the Global Commission on the Stability of Cyberspace has published several documents, including the "Norm to Protect the Public Core," which aims to protect critical internet infrastructure from cyber attacks. These initiatives highlight the importance of international cooperation and the role of international institutions in addressing the challenges posed by cyberpolitics.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of cyberpolitics in international relations. By examining theoretical frameworks, research methods, and policy implications, readers will gain a deeper insight into the complexities of this emerging field and its impact on global politics.


## Chapter 5: Comparative Analysis and Cases in Context

### Section 5.1 International Institutional Challenges Re-Visited: Sovereign States, Private Order, ad hoc Arrangements

In the previous chapters, we have discussed the theoretical frameworks and methods used to understand cyberpolitics in international relations. In this section, we will revisit the challenges faced by international institutions in governing cyber activities. As technology continues to advance and the use of cyberspace becomes more prevalent in international relations, it is crucial to examine the challenges faced by international institutions in regulating and governing this domain.

One of the main challenges faced by international institutions in cyber governance is the issue of sovereignty. In the traditional sense, sovereignty refers to a state's supreme authority over its territory and people. However, in the context of cyberspace, the concept of sovereignty becomes more complex. With the borderless nature of the internet, it becomes challenging to determine which state has jurisdiction over cyber activities. This creates a challenge for international institutions in enforcing regulations and laws in cyberspace.

Another challenge is the emergence of private order in cyberspace. Private companies and organizations play a significant role in the development and maintenance of the internet. This creates a power dynamic where these private entities have control over critical infrastructure and data. As a result, international institutions may struggle to regulate and govern these private actors, leading to potential gaps in cyber governance.

Ad hoc arrangements also pose a challenge for international institutions in governing cyberspace. With the rapid pace of technological advancements, new cyber threats and challenges emerge constantly. This requires international institutions to adapt and create new arrangements to address these challenges. However, the process of creating and implementing these arrangements can be slow and may not keep up with the pace of technological change.

These challenges highlight the need for international institutions to continuously reassess and adapt their approaches to governing cyberspace. As technology continues to evolve, it is crucial for international institutions to stay updated and work together to address the challenges posed by cyberspace. In the next section, we will explore specific challenges faced by international institutions in cyber governance.


## Chapter 5: Comparative Analysis and Cases in Context

### Section 5.1 International Institutional Challenges Re-Visited: Sovereign States, Private Order, ad hoc Arrangements

In the previous chapters, we have discussed the theoretical frameworks and methods used to understand cyberpolitics in international relations. In this section, we will revisit the challenges faced by international institutions in governing cyber activities. As technology continues to advance and the use of cyberspace becomes more prevalent in international relations, it is crucial to examine the challenges faced by international institutions in regulating and governing this domain.

One of the main challenges faced by international institutions in cyber governance is the issue of sovereignty. In the traditional sense, sovereignty refers to a state's supreme authority over its territory and people. However, in the context of cyberspace, the concept of sovereignty becomes more complex. With the borderless nature of the internet, it becomes challenging to determine which state has jurisdiction over cyber activities. This creates a challenge for international institutions in enforcing regulations and laws in cyberspace.

Moreover, the issue of sovereignty is further complicated by the involvement of non-state actors in cyberspace. Private companies and organizations play a significant role in the development and maintenance of the internet. This creates a power dynamic where these private entities have control over critical infrastructure and data. As a result, international institutions may struggle to regulate and govern these private actors, leading to potential gaps in cyber governance.

Another challenge is the emergence of private order in cyberspace. Private companies and organizations play a significant role in the development and maintenance of the internet. This creates a power dynamic where these private entities have control over critical infrastructure and data. As a result, international institutions may struggle to regulate and govern these private actors, leading to potential gaps in cyber governance.

Ad hoc arrangements also pose a challenge for international institutions in governing cyberspace. With the rapid pace of technological advancements, new cyber threats and challenges emerge constantly. This requires international institutions to adapt and create new arrangements to address these challenges. However, the process of creating and implementing these arrangements can be slow and cumbersome, leaving room for potential vulnerabilities in cyber governance.

To better understand these challenges, it is essential to examine case studies of international institutions in cyber governance. One such case study is the Global Commission on Internet Governance (GCIG). Launched in 2014, the GCIG was formed to make recommendations about the future of global internet governance. It is considered one of the international initiatives that facilitate effective cooperation between relevant international actors, particularly according to the principles of internet governance.

The GCIG's research advisory network, led by Laura DeNardis, produces original research on Internet Governance topics such as the dark web, cybersecurity, and internet freedom. For instance, a research published in January 2017 entitled "Who Runs the Internet? The Global Multi-stakeholder Model of Internet Governance" described a "multistakeholder" framework wherein the management of the global Internet architecture is in the hands of a cluster of international stakeholders such as industry, academic and non-governmental actors. However, there is criticism from some countries against the current attempts at a multistakeholder process that cite how these appear to be led by Western nations.

In addition to the GCIG, the Global Commission on the Stability of Cyberspace (GCSC) is another international institution that has published several documents related to cyber governance. These include the "Norm to Protect the Public Core" and seven subsequent norms. The GCSC also defined the "Public Core" to which the norm applies, with the effort divided into two working groups, one to specify what actions should be precluded and the other to specify which infrastructures are deemed most worthy of protection.

These case studies highlight the challenges faced by international institutions in governing cyberspace and the efforts being made to address them. As technology continues to advance and the use of cyberspace becomes more prevalent in international relations, it is crucial for international institutions to adapt and evolve to effectively regulate and govern this domain. 


## Chapter 5: Comparative Analysis and Cases in Context

### Section: 5.2 Global Agenda- Emergent Accord & New Discord:

### Subsection (optional): 5.2a Current Global Agenda in Cyber Politics

In the previous section, we discussed the challenges faced by international institutions in governing cyber activities. In this section, we will examine the current global agenda in cyber politics and how it is shaping the landscape of international relations.

One of the key issues on the global agenda in cyber politics is the need for international cooperation and coordination in addressing cyber threats. As technology continues to advance, cyber threats have become more sophisticated and widespread, posing a significant challenge to global security. In response, international institutions have been working towards developing frameworks and agreements to facilitate cooperation and information sharing among states.

One notable example is the International Multilateral Partnership Against Cyber Threats, which aims to promote collaboration and coordination among states in addressing cyber threats. This partnership has also led to the establishment of the Global Commission on Internet Governance, which works towards developing recommendations for the future of global internet governance.

Another important aspect of the current global agenda in cyber politics is the issue of internet governance. With the increasing role of the internet in international relations, there has been a growing debate on how to effectively govern this domain. The Global Commission on Internet Governance, chaired by Carl Bildt, has been at the forefront of this discussion, advocating for a multi-stakeholder approach to internet governance.

However, there are also emerging challenges and discord in the global agenda for cyber politics. One of the main sources of discord is the issue of sovereignty in cyberspace. As mentioned earlier, the borderless nature of the internet makes it difficult to determine jurisdiction and enforce regulations. This has led to tensions between states, particularly in cases where cyber attacks originate from one state but target another.

Moreover, the involvement of non-state actors in cyberspace has also created challenges in the global agenda for cyber politics. Private companies and organizations have significant control over critical infrastructure and data, making it difficult for international institutions to regulate and govern their actions. This has led to concerns about the potential misuse of this power and the need for greater accountability and oversight.

In conclusion, the current global agenda in cyber politics is focused on promoting international cooperation and addressing challenges in internet governance. However, there are also emerging challenges and discord that must be addressed to effectively govern cyberspace and ensure global security. 


## Chapter 5: Comparative Analysis and Cases in Context

### Section: 5.2 Global Agenda- Emergent Accord & New Discord:

### Subsection (optional): 5.2b Emerging Accords and New Discord in Cyber Politics

In the previous section, we discussed the current global agenda in cyber politics and the challenges faced by international institutions in governing cyber activities. In this section, we will delve deeper into the emerging accords and new discord in cyber politics, and how they are shaping the landscape of international relations.

One of the key emerging accords in cyber politics is the increasing recognition of the need for international cooperation and coordination in addressing cyber threats. As technology continues to advance, cyber threats have become more sophisticated and widespread, posing a significant challenge to global security. In response, international institutions have been working towards developing frameworks and agreements to facilitate cooperation and information sharing among states.

One notable example is the International Multilateral Partnership Against Cyber Threats, which aims to promote collaboration and coordination among states in addressing cyber threats. This partnership has also led to the establishment of the Global Commission on Internet Governance, which works towards developing recommendations for the future of global internet governance.

Another important aspect of the emerging accords in cyber politics is the increasing recognition of the role of non-state actors in cyber activities. With the rise of hacktivism, cyber espionage, and cyber terrorism, it has become clear that non-state actors can have a significant impact on international relations through their actions in cyberspace. This has led to a shift in focus towards including non-state actors in discussions and agreements related to cyber governance.

However, there are also new sources of discord in the global agenda for cyber politics. One of the main sources of discord is the issue of sovereignty in cyberspace. As mentioned earlier, the borderless nature of the internet makes it difficult to determine jurisdiction and responsibility for cyber attacks. This has led to debates and disagreements over the role of states in regulating and controlling cyberspace.

Another source of discord is the increasing use of cyber tools for political purposes. With the rise of social media and online propaganda, states are using cyber tools to influence public opinion and interfere in the political processes of other countries. This has led to concerns over the potential for cyber attacks to be used as a tool for political manipulation and interference in the internal affairs of other states.

In conclusion, the global agenda for cyber politics is constantly evolving, with emerging accords and new sources of discord shaping the landscape of international relations. As technology continues to advance and the role of cyberspace in international relations becomes more prominent, it is crucial for international institutions to adapt and address these emerging challenges in order to maintain global security and stability.


## Chapter 5: Comparative Analysis and Cases in Context:

### Section: 5.2 Global Agenda- Emergent Accord & New Discord:

### Subsection (optional): 5.2c Case Studies of Global Agenda in Cyber Politics

In the previous section, we discussed the current global agenda in cyber politics and the challenges faced by international institutions in governing cyber activities. In this section, we will examine case studies that illustrate the emerging accords and new discord in cyber politics, and how they are shaping the landscape of international relations.

One of the key case studies in the emerging accords of cyber politics is the International Multilateral Partnership Against Cyber Threats. This partnership, formed in 2014, aims to promote collaboration and coordination among states in addressing cyber threats. It has been successful in facilitating information sharing and cooperation among member states, leading to a more coordinated response to cyber threats.

Another important case study is the Global Commission on Internet Governance, which was launched in 2014 by two think tanks, the Canadian Centre for International Governance Innovation and UK-based Chatham House. This commission, chaired by Carl Bildt, works towards developing recommendations for the future of global internet governance. It is considered one of the international initiatives that facilitate effective cooperation between relevant international actors, particularly according to the principles of internet governance.

However, there are also new sources of discord in the global agenda for cyber politics. One example is the criticism from some countries against the current attempts at a multistakeholder process in internet governance. These countries argue that the process is led by Western nations and does not adequately represent the interests of all stakeholders. This has led to tensions and disagreements in international discussions on cyber governance.

Another case study of new discord in cyber politics is the Council on Foreign Relations task force report no. 80 (2022). This report, completed in May 2022, recommends that the U.S. reconsider its cyber, digital trade, and online freedom policies, which have been championing a free and open internet. The report argues that these policies have failed and calls for a reassessment of the U.S.'s approach to cyber issues.

In addition, the recent NCSC ransomware speech at Tel Aviv Cyber Week (2022) also highlights the new discord in cyber politics. During this speech, the 12th annual event was disrupted by a ransomware attack, demonstrating the vulnerability of critical infrastructure to cyber threats. This incident has raised concerns about the need for stronger cybersecurity measures and international cooperation in addressing cyber threats.

Overall, these case studies illustrate the complex and evolving nature of the global agenda in cyber politics. While there are emerging accords and efforts towards international cooperation, there are also new sources of discord and challenges that must be addressed in order to effectively govern cyber activities in the international arena. 


### Section: 5.3 Alternative Futures- Vision, Principles, Trajectories:

In this section, we will explore alternative futures for cyber politics, examining different visions, principles, and trajectories that may shape the landscape of international relations in the digital age. As technology continues to advance and shape our world, it is important to consider the potential implications for global governance and cooperation.

#### "Future Visions for Cyber Politics"

One potential future vision for cyber politics is a world where technology is used to enhance and promote democracy and human rights. This vision is based on the belief that access to information and communication technologies can empower individuals and promote transparency and accountability in government. This vision aligns with the principles of open and inclusive governance, where all stakeholders have a voice in decision-making processes.

Another potential future vision is a world where cyber threats and attacks are constantly evolving, requiring constant adaptation and cooperation among states. This vision highlights the need for strong international partnerships and coordination in addressing cyber threats. It also emphasizes the importance of developing and implementing effective policies and regulations to protect against cyber attacks.

#### "Principles for Cyber Politics"

In order to achieve these future visions, certain principles must be upheld in cyber politics. These principles include transparency, accountability, and inclusivity. Transparency is crucial in ensuring that all stakeholders have access to information and can hold governments and institutions accountable for their actions. Accountability is necessary to ensure that those responsible for cyber attacks are held responsible and that appropriate measures are taken to prevent future attacks. Inclusivity is important in promoting equal participation and representation in decision-making processes, especially for marginalized groups.

#### "Trajectories for Cyber Politics"

The trajectory of cyber politics will be heavily influenced by the actions and decisions of key actors, such as governments, international organizations, and private companies. One potential trajectory is towards increased cooperation and collaboration among states in addressing cyber threats. This could involve the development of international agreements and norms, as well as the sharing of information and resources.

Another potential trajectory is towards increased regulation and control of the internet by governments. This could lead to restrictions on freedom of expression and access to information, as well as potential conflicts between states with different approaches to internet governance.

Ultimately, the future of cyber politics will depend on the choices and actions of individuals and institutions. It is important for all stakeholders to consider the potential consequences of their decisions and work towards a future that promotes democracy, human rights, and global cooperation.


### Section: 5.3 Alternative Futures- Vision, Principles, Trajectories:

In this section, we will explore alternative futures for cyber politics, examining different visions, principles, and trajectories that may shape the landscape of international relations in the digital age. As technology continues to advance and shape our world, it is important to consider the potential implications for global governance and cooperation.

#### "Future Visions for Cyber Politics"

One potential future vision for cyber politics is a world where technology is used to enhance and promote democracy and human rights. This vision is based on the belief that access to information and communication technologies can empower individuals and promote transparency and accountability in government. This vision aligns with the principles of open and inclusive governance, where all stakeholders have a voice in decision-making processes.

This vision is supported by the underlying pillars of digital civics, which include philosophy, history, ethics, and civics. The philosophy of information, as described by Luciano Floridi, recognizes the transformative power of technology and the impact it has on human behavior. Drawing from media ecology and classical scholarship, the historical perspective of digital civics acknowledges the long tradition of addressing challenges brought about by technological advancements. The ethical pillar, particularly virtue ethics, emphasizes the importance of responding to these changes in a morally sound and rigorous manner. Finally, the civic pillar, which includes the Universal Declaration of Human Rights, recognizes the importance of balancing the public and private personas in the digital age.

Another potential future vision is a world where cyber threats and attacks are constantly evolving, requiring constant adaptation and cooperation among states. This vision highlights the need for strong international partnerships and coordination in addressing cyber threats. It also emphasizes the importance of developing and implementing effective policies and regulations to protect against cyber attacks.

#### "Principles for Cyber Politics"

In order to achieve these future visions, certain principles must be upheld in cyber politics. These principles include transparency, accountability, and inclusivity. Transparency is crucial in ensuring that all stakeholders have access to information and can hold governments and institutions accountable for their actions. Accountability is necessary to ensure that those responsible for cyber attacks are held responsible and that appropriate measures are taken to prevent future attacks. Inclusivity is important in promoting equal participation and representation in decision-making processes, especially for marginalized communities.

To further support these principles, digital civics also identifies four key concepts that are grounded in the informational nature of reality. These concepts include acknowledging the transformations brought about by technology, responding to these changes in ethical and rigorous ways, drawing from historical traditions, and recognizing the importance of information in shaping our world.

#### "Trajectories for Cyber Politics"

As technology continues to advance, it is important to consider the potential trajectories for cyber politics. One potential trajectory is the development of a global information ethics, built upon the principles of digital civics and virtue ethics. This would require international cooperation and coordination in addressing ethical issues in the digital age.

Another trajectory is the potential for increased government surveillance and control in the name of national security. This could lead to a decrease in transparency and accountability, as well as a violation of individual privacy rights. It is important for governments to balance security concerns with the protection of individual rights and freedoms.

In conclusion, the future of cyber politics is constantly evolving and it is important for international relations to adapt and respond to these changes. By upholding principles of transparency, accountability, and inclusivity, and drawing from the pillars and key concepts of digital civics, we can work towards a future where technology is used to promote democracy, human rights, and global cooperation. 


### Section: 5.3 Alternative Futures- Vision, Principles, Trajectories:

In this section, we will explore alternative futures for cyber politics, examining different visions, principles, and trajectories that may shape the landscape of international relations in the digital age. As technology continues to advance and shape our world, it is important to consider the potential implications for global governance and cooperation.

#### "Future Visions for Cyber Politics"

One potential future vision for cyber politics is a world where technology is used to enhance and promote democracy and human rights. This vision is based on the belief that access to information and communication technologies can empower individuals and promote transparency and accountability in government. This vision aligns with the principles of open and inclusive governance, where all stakeholders have a voice in decision-making processes.

This vision is supported by the underlying pillars of digital civics, which include philosophy, history, ethics, and civics. The philosophy of information, as described by Luciano Floridi, recognizes the transformative power of technology and the impact it has on human behavior. Drawing from media ecology and classical scholarship, the historical perspective of digital civics acknowledges the long tradition of addressing challenges brought about by technological advancements. The ethical pillar, particularly virtue ethics, emphasizes the importance of responding to these changes in a morally sound and rigorous manner. Finally, the civic pillar, which includes the Universal Declaration of Human Rights, recognizes the importance of balancing the public and private personas in the digital age.

Another potential future vision is a world where cyber threats and attacks are constantly evolving, requiring constant adaptation and cooperation among states. This vision highlights the need for strong international partnerships and coordination in addressing cyber threats. However, this vision also raises concerns about the potential for increased surveillance and censorship in the name of national security. This could lead to a world where individual privacy and freedom of expression are compromised in the name of protecting against cyber threats.

#### "Predicted Trajectories for Cyber Politics"

In order to better understand the potential trajectories for cyber politics, it is important to analyze current trends and developments in the field. One predicted trajectory is the continued rise of computational politics, where computer science and political science intersect to study and address political issues. This field utilizes computational methods, such as data analysis and prediction tools, to provide solutions to political problems. With the increasing availability of data from social media and other online sources, computational politics is becoming an increasingly important tool for understanding and influencing political behavior.

Another predicted trajectory is the growing importance of international partnerships and cooperation in addressing cyber threats. As technology continues to advance and cyber attacks become more sophisticated, no single country can effectively combat these threats alone. This highlights the need for multilateral partnerships and agreements to establish norms and regulations for cyber activities. The International Multilateral Partnership Against Cyber Threats is one example of such a partnership, working towards promoting international cooperation and coordination in addressing cyber threats.

However, there are also potential challenges and obstacles that could impact the trajectory of cyber politics. One major concern is the digital divide, where certain countries or groups have limited access to technology and are therefore at a disadvantage in the digital world. This could lead to unequal power dynamics and further exacerbate existing inequalities in international relations.

In conclusion, the future of cyber politics is complex and uncertain, with multiple potential trajectories and outcomes. It is important for policymakers and researchers to consider these alternative futures and work towards promoting a vision of cyber politics that prioritizes democracy, human rights, and international cooperation. 


### Section: 5.4 The Impact of Non-State Actors on International Cyber Politics:

Non-state actors, such as private companies, non-governmental organizations, and individuals, play a significant role in shaping international cyber politics. In this section, we will explore the various ways in which these actors influence the landscape of cyber politics and the potential implications for global governance and cooperation.

#### "Role of Non-State Actors in Cyber Politics"

Non-state actors have become increasingly involved in cyber politics, both as targets and perpetrators of cyber attacks, and as key players in shaping policies and regulations. Private companies, in particular, have a significant impact on the development and implementation of technology, as they often have the resources and expertise to create and maintain digital infrastructure. This influence can be seen in the development of self-sovereign identity (SSI) technology.

SSI is a value-laden technology that allows individuals to have control over their digital identities. However, its implementation can vary significantly, and different actors may embed their own goals and intentions into the technology. For example, private companies may prioritize profit and data collection, while non-governmental organizations may prioritize privacy and security. This can lead to semantic confusion, as the term "self-sovereign identity" may create expectations of absolute control and ownership over digital identities, which may not align with the reality of complex technical infrastructure and legal frameworks.

Furthermore, the role of non-state actors in cyber politics raises concerns about digital literacy and social inequalities. SSI assumes reliable internet connectivity, access to compatible devices, and proficiency in navigating digital systems. This can exclude marginalized populations, such as the elderly or individuals in developing regions, from accessing the benefits of SSI. As such, it is crucial for non-state actors to consider the potential implications of their actions on global governance and cooperation.

In addition to their impact on technology, non-state actors also play a role in shaping policies and regulations in cyberspace. The government's regulatory role in cyberspace is complicated, as some view it as a virtual space that should remain free of government intervention. However, others argue that the government has a crucial role in protecting national infrastructure and regulating companies and organizations to prevent cyber attacks.

In conclusion, non-state actors have a significant impact on international cyber politics, both in terms of technology development and policy-making. As technology continues to advance and shape our world, it is important for these actors to consider the potential implications of their actions on global governance and cooperation. 


### Section: 5.4 The Impact of Non-State Actors on International Cyber Politics:

Non-state actors, such as private companies, non-governmental organizations, and individuals, play a significant role in shaping international cyber politics. In this section, we will explore the various ways in which these actors influence the landscape of cyber politics and the potential implications for global governance and cooperation.

#### "Impact of Non-State Actors on Cyber Politics"

Non-state actors have become increasingly involved in cyber politics, both as targets and perpetrators of cyber attacks, and as key players in shaping policies and regulations. Private companies, in particular, have a significant impact on the development and implementation of technology, as they often have the resources and expertise to create and maintain digital infrastructure.

One area where non-state actors have had a significant impact is in the development of self-sovereign identity (SSI) technology. SSI is a value-laden technology that allows individuals to have control over their digital identities. However, its implementation can vary significantly, and different actors may embed their own goals and intentions into the technology. For example, private companies may prioritize profit and data collection, while non-governmental organizations may prioritize privacy and security. This can lead to semantic confusion, as the term "self-sovereign identity" may create expectations of absolute control and ownership over digital identities, which may not align with the reality of complex technical infrastructure and legal frameworks.

Furthermore, the role of non-state actors in cyber politics raises concerns about digital literacy and social inequalities. SSI assumes reliable internet connectivity, access to compatible devices, and proficiency in navigating digital systems. This can exclude marginalized populations, such as the elderly or individuals in developing regions, from accessing the benefits of SSI. As such, it is crucial for policymakers to consider the potential impact of SSI on different populations and ensure that measures are in place to address any potential inequalities.

In addition to shaping technology and policies, non-state actors also play a significant role in cyber attacks and cyber warfare. Private companies may be targeted by state-sponsored cyber attacks, as seen in the case of the 2014 Sony Pictures hack, where North Korea was suspected of targeting the company in response to the release of a film depicting the assassination of their leader. Non-governmental organizations may also be targeted for their political or social activism, as seen in the case of the 2016 Democratic National Committee hack, where Russian hackers targeted the organization in an attempt to influence the US presidential election.

The involvement of non-state actors in cyber attacks raises questions about accountability and responsibility. Unlike state actors, non-state actors do not have the same level of accountability and may not be subject to the same consequences for their actions. This can create challenges in terms of international cooperation and response to cyber attacks, as there may not be clear lines of responsibility.

In conclusion, non-state actors have a significant impact on international cyber politics, from shaping technology and policies to being involved in cyber attacks. As technology continues to advance and non-state actors become more involved in cyber politics, it is crucial for policymakers to consider their role and potential implications for global governance and cooperation. 


### Section: 5.4 The Impact of Non-State Actors on International Cyber Politics:

Non-state actors, such as private companies, non-governmental organizations, and individuals, play a significant role in shaping international cyber politics. In this section, we will explore the various ways in which these actors influence the landscape of cyber politics and the potential implications for global governance and cooperation.

#### "Impact of Non-State Actors on Cyber Politics"

Non-state actors have become increasingly involved in cyber politics, both as targets and perpetrators of cyber attacks, and as key players in shaping policies and regulations. Private companies, in particular, have a significant impact on the development and implementation of technology, as they often have the resources and expertise to create and maintain digital infrastructure.

One area where non-state actors have had a significant impact is in the development of self-sovereign identity (SSI) technology. SSI is a value-laden technology that allows individuals to have control over their digital identities. However, its implementation can vary significantly, and different actors may embed their own goals and intentions into the technology. For example, private companies may prioritize profit and data collection, while non-governmental organizations may prioritize privacy and security. This can lead to semantic confusion, as the term "self-sovereign identity" may create expectations of absolute control and ownership over digital identities, which may not align with the reality of complex technical infrastructure and legal frameworks.

Furthermore, the role of non-state actors in cyber politics raises concerns about digital literacy and social inequalities. SSI assumes reliable internet connectivity, access to compatible devices, and proficiency in navigating digital systems. This can exclude marginalized populations, such as the elderly or individuals in developing regions, from accessing the benefits of SSI. This exclusion can further exacerbate existing social inequalities and create a digital divide between those who have access to SSI and those who do not.

#### "Case Studies of Non-State Actors in Cyber Politics"

To better understand the impact of non-state actors on international cyber politics, it is essential to examine case studies of their involvement. One such case study is the development of the Open Source Enterprise (OSE) by the United States intelligence agencies. The OSE is a collaborative effort between government agencies, private companies, and academic institutions to gather and analyze open-source intelligence. This partnership highlights the significant role that private companies play in shaping cyber politics, as they provide the technology and expertise necessary for the OSE's success.

Another case study is the implementation of self-sovereign identity by various non-state actors. For example, the International Multilateral Partnership Against Cyber Threats (IMPACT) has developed its own SSI framework, which prioritizes privacy and security. In contrast, private companies, such as Microsoft and IBM, have also implemented SSI technology, but with a focus on data collection and profit. These differing implementations of SSI highlight the potential for conflicting interests and goals among non-state actors in shaping cyber politics.

#### "Challenges and Opportunities for Global Governance and Cooperation"

The involvement of non-state actors in cyber politics presents both challenges and opportunities for global governance and cooperation. On one hand, their involvement can lead to conflicting interests and goals, making it difficult to establish unified policies and regulations. On the other hand, their expertise and resources can also contribute to the development of effective solutions to cyber threats.

To address these challenges and harness the opportunities presented by non-state actors, it is crucial to promote digital civics. Digital civics, as defined by Clements, involves four underlying pillars: philosophy, history, ethics, and technology. By grounding digital civics in these pillars, we can promote a more holistic and ethical approach to cyber politics, taking into account the diverse perspectives and interests of non-state actors.

In conclusion, non-state actors play a significant role in shaping international cyber politics, and their involvement presents both challenges and opportunities for global governance and cooperation. By examining case studies and promoting digital civics, we can better understand and navigate the impact of non-state actors in this complex and ever-evolving landscape.

In this chapter, we have explored the use of comparative analysis and case studies in the context of cyberpolitics in international relations. We have seen how these methods can be applied to better understand the complex and ever-evolving landscape of cyberpolitics, and how they can inform policy decisions.

Through comparative analysis, we have been able to identify patterns and trends across different countries and regions, shedding light on the similarities and differences in their approaches to cyberpolitics. This has allowed us to gain a deeper understanding of the factors that influence cyberpolitics and how they can impact international relations.

Case studies have also been a valuable tool in our exploration of cyberpolitics. By examining specific incidents and events, we have been able to analyze the strategies and tactics used by different actors in the cyber realm. This has provided us with valuable insights into the motivations and goals of these actors, as well as the potential consequences of their actions.

Overall, the use of comparative analysis and case studies has greatly enhanced our understanding of cyberpolitics in international relations. By combining these methods with existing theories and frameworks, we have been able to develop a more comprehensive and nuanced understanding of this complex and rapidly evolving field.

## Chapter: Cyberpolitics in International Relations: Theory, Methods, Policy

### Introduction:

In today's interconnected world, the use of technology and the internet has become an integral part of our daily lives. This has also extended to the realm of international relations, where the use of cyberspace has become a crucial aspect of state interactions. The increasing reliance on cyberspace has led to the emergence of cyber norms and rules, which govern the behavior of states in the digital realm. In this chapter, we will explore the evolution of these norms and rules, and how they have shaped the landscape of cyberpolitics in international relations.

The chapter will begin by providing a brief overview of the concept of cyber norms and rules, and their significance in the context of international relations. We will then delve into the historical evolution of these norms and rules, tracing their origins from the early days of the internet to the present day. This will include an examination of key events and developments that have influenced the formation of cyber norms and rules, such as cyber attacks, data breaches, and international agreements.

Furthermore, the chapter will also explore the various methods used to establish and enforce cyber norms and rules. This will include an analysis of the role of international organizations, such as the United Nations and the International Telecommunication Union, in promoting and regulating cyber activities. We will also examine the role of state actors, non-state actors, and other stakeholders in shaping the development of cyber norms and rules.

Finally, the chapter will discuss the policy implications of the evolving cyber norms and rules in international relations. This will include an examination of the challenges and opportunities presented by the current state of cyber norms and rules, and the potential impact on state behavior and global governance. We will also explore potential future developments and their potential impact on the international cyber landscape.

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the evolution of cyber norms and rules in international relations. By examining the historical development, methods of establishment, and policy implications, we hope to shed light on the complex and ever-changing nature of cyberpolitics in the international arena. 


## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules

### Section 6.1: The Role of International Organizations in Cyber Governance

International organizations play a crucial role in the development and enforcement of cyber norms and rules. These organizations serve as platforms for international cooperation and coordination, and their efforts have been instrumental in shaping the landscape of cyberpolitics in international relations.

One of the key international organizations involved in cyber governance is the Global Commission on the Stability of Cyberspace (GCSC). Established in 2017, the GCSC is an independent body composed of experts from various fields, including government, academia, and the private sector. Its primary goal is to promote international cooperation and stability in cyberspace through the development of norms and rules.

The GCSC has published several documents related to cyber norms and rules, including the "Norm to Protect the Public Core" and the "Definition of the Public Core, to which the Norm Applies". These documents provide a standardized description of the critical elements of the internet that should be protected from cyber attacks and interference by state actors. The GCSC's efforts have been recognized and utilized by other international organizations, such as the Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).

In addition to these documents, the GCSC has also released a statement on the interpretation of the norm on non-interference with the public core. This statement reaffirms the GCSC's belief in the multistakeholder model of internet governance and the role of the private sector in operating the internet's critical infrastructure. It also addresses concerns raised by Russia regarding the existing internet governance and operational model.

Apart from the GCSC, other international organizations, such as the United Nations and the International Telecommunication Union, have also played a significant role in promoting and regulating cyber activities. The United Nations has established several initiatives, such as the Group of Governmental Experts on Developments in the Field of Information and Telecommunications in the Context of International Security, to address issues related to cyber norms and rules. The International Telecommunication Union has also developed guidelines and recommendations for member states to enhance cybersecurity and promote responsible behavior in cyberspace.

The involvement of international organizations in cyber governance has not been without challenges. One of the main challenges is the lack of a universal consensus on cyber norms and rules. Different countries may have varying perspectives and interests, making it difficult to reach a consensus on certain issues. Additionally, the fast-paced nature of technology and the internet makes it challenging for international organizations to keep up with the constantly evolving cyber landscape.

Despite these challenges, the role of international organizations in cyber governance remains crucial. Their efforts in promoting and regulating cyber activities have helped establish a framework for responsible behavior in cyberspace and have contributed to the stability of the internet. As technology continues to advance, it is essential for international organizations to adapt and evolve their approaches to effectively address emerging cyber threats and challenges.


## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules

### Section 6.1: The Role of International Organizations in Cyber Governance

International organizations play a crucial role in the development and enforcement of cyber norms and rules. These organizations serve as platforms for international cooperation and coordination, and their efforts have been instrumental in shaping the landscape of cyberpolitics in international relations.

One of the key international organizations involved in cyber governance is the Global Commission on the Stability of Cyberspace (GCSC). Established in 2017, the GCSC is an independent body composed of experts from various fields, including government, academia, and the private sector. Its primary goal is to promote international cooperation and stability in cyberspace through the development of norms and rules.

The GCSC has published several documents related to cyber norms and rules, including the "Norm to Protect the Public Core" and the "Definition of the Public Core, to which the Norm Applies". These documents provide a standardized description of the critical elements of the internet that should be protected from cyber attacks and interference by state actors. The GCSC's efforts have been recognized and utilized by other international organizations, such as the Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).

In addition to these documents, the GCSC has also released a statement on the interpretation of the norm on non-interference with the public core. This statement reaffirms the GCSC's belief in the multistakeholder model of internet governance and the role of the private sector in operating the internet's critical infrastructure. It also addresses concerns raised by Russia regarding the existing internet governance and operational model.

Apart from the GCSC, other international organizations, such as the United Nations and the International Telecommunication Union, have also played a significant role in promoting cyber norms and rules. These organizations have developed various initiatives and frameworks to address cyber threats and promote responsible behavior in cyberspace.

One example is the United Nations Group of Governmental Experts (UN GGE) on Developments in the Field of Information and Telecommunications in the Context of International Security. This group, composed of experts from various countries, has produced several reports on the application of international law to cyberspace and the development of norms for responsible state behavior in cyberspace.

Another example is the International Telecommunication Union (ITU), a specialized agency of the United Nations responsible for information and communication technologies. The ITU has developed the Global Cybersecurity Index (GCI), which measures the commitment of countries to cybersecurity and provides a framework for international cooperation in this area.

The efforts of these international organizations have been crucial in promoting the development of cyber norms and rules at the international level. By providing a platform for cooperation and coordination, these organizations have helped to shape the global discourse on cyber governance and promote responsible behavior in cyberspace.

### Subsection: 6.1b Impact of International Organizations on Cyber Norms and Rules

The impact of international organizations on cyber norms and rules can be seen in the widespread adoption and implementation of their initiatives and frameworks. For example, the GCSC's "Norm to Protect the Public Core" has been endorsed by numerous countries and organizations, including the European Union and the United Nations.

Moreover, the efforts of international organizations have also led to the development of new norms and rules in the field of cyber governance. For instance, the UN GGE's reports have contributed to the development of norms for responsible state behavior in cyberspace, such as the norm of non-interference in the internal affairs of other states.

Furthermore, international organizations have also played a crucial role in promoting compliance with cyber norms and rules. Through their monitoring and reporting mechanisms, these organizations have been able to identify and address violations of cyber norms and rules, thereby promoting their effectiveness and legitimacy.

In conclusion, the role of international organizations in cyber governance cannot be overstated. These organizations have been instrumental in promoting the development, adoption, and implementation of cyber norms and rules at the international level. As the cyber landscape continues to evolve, the role of international organizations will remain crucial in ensuring stability and security in cyberspace.


## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules

### Section 6.1: The Role of International Organizations in Cyber Governance

International organizations play a crucial role in the development and enforcement of cyber norms and rules. These organizations serve as platforms for international cooperation and coordination, and their efforts have been instrumental in shaping the landscape of cyberpolitics in international relations.

One of the key international organizations involved in cyber governance is the Global Commission on Internet Governance (GCIG). Established in 2014, the GCIG is an independent body composed of experts from various fields, including government, academia, and the private sector. Its primary goal is to make recommendations about the future of global internet governance and promote effective cooperation between relevant international actors.

The GCIG's research advisory network, led by Laura DeNardis, produces original research on internet governance topics such as the dark web, cybersecurity, and internet freedom. For instance, a research published in January 2017 entitled "Who Runs the Internet? The Global Multi-stakeholder Model of Internet Governance" described a "multistakeholder" framework wherein the management of the global internet architecture is in the hands of a cluster of international stakeholders such as industry, academic, and non-governmental actors. This research has been influential in shaping the GCIG's approach to cyber governance.

In addition to its research efforts, the GCIG has also published several documents related to cyber norms and rules. These include the "Norm to Protect the Public Core" and the "Definition of the Public Core, to which the Norm Applies". These documents provide a standardized description of the critical elements of the internet that should be protected from cyber attacks and interference by state actors. The GCIG's efforts have been recognized and utilized by other international organizations, such as the Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).

Apart from these documents, the GCIG has also released a statement on the interpretation of the norm on non-interference with the public core. This statement reaffirms the GCIG's belief in the multistakeholder model of internet governance and the role of the private sector in operating the internet's critical infrastructure. It also addresses concerns raised by some countries against the current attempts at a multistakeholder process, citing how these appear to be led by Western nations.

In addition to the GCIG, other international organizations, such as the United Nations and the International Telecommunication Union, have also played a significant role in promoting cyber norms and rules. For example, the United Nations has established the Group of Governmental Experts (GGE) on Developments in the Field of Information and Telecommunications in the Context of International Security, which has produced several reports on the application of international law to cyberspace. The International Telecommunication Union has also developed the Global Cybersecurity Index, which measures the commitment of countries to cybersecurity and provides a framework for international cooperation.

Overall, international organizations play a crucial role in the development and enforcement of cyber norms and rules. Their efforts have been instrumental in promoting international cooperation and stability in cyberspace, and their work continues to shape the evolving landscape of cyberpolitics in international relations. 


## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules

### Section 6.2: Case Studies: Cyber Politics in Different Regions of the World

As the internet continues to play an increasingly important role in international relations, it is essential to examine how different regions of the world are approaching cyber politics. In this section, we will explore the unique challenges and approaches to cyber governance in North America.

### Subsection 6.2a: Cyber Politics in North America

North America, consisting of the United States, Canada, and Mexico, has been at the forefront of the development and use of cyberspace. With advanced technological infrastructure and a high level of internet penetration, the region has become a major player in the global digital economy. However, this also makes it a prime target for cyber attacks and raises concerns about the protection of critical infrastructure and personal data.

The United States, as a global superpower, has been a key player in shaping cyber norms and rules. The country has taken a multi-stakeholder approach to cyber governance, involving government, industry, academia, and civil society in decision-making processes. This approach has been heavily influenced by the research and recommendations of the Global Commission on Internet Governance (GCIG), which has highlighted the importance of collaboration between different stakeholders in managing the internet.

One of the key challenges in North America is the protection of personal data and privacy. With the rise of social media and online platforms, there has been a growing concern about the collection and use of personal data by companies and governments. In response, the United States has implemented various laws and regulations, such as the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) and the California Consumer Privacy Act (CCPA), to protect the privacy of its citizens.

Canada, on the other hand, has taken a more proactive approach to cyber governance. In 2010, the country established the Canadian Cyber Incident Response Centre (CCIRC) to coordinate and respond to cyber threats. The CCIRC works closely with government agencies, the private sector, and international partners to prevent and mitigate cyber attacks. Additionally, Canada has also implemented the Personal Information Protection and Electronic Documents Act (PIPEDA) to regulate the collection, use, and disclosure of personal information by private sector organizations.

Mexico, while still developing its cyber infrastructure, has also taken steps towards cyber governance. In 2017, the country passed the General Law on the Protection of Personal Data (LGPD) to regulate the collection and use of personal data by both public and private entities. Mexico has also established the National Cybersecurity System (SNS) to coordinate efforts between government agencies and the private sector in responding to cyber threats.

In conclusion, North America has made significant progress in developing and implementing cyber norms and rules. However, as technology continues to evolve, it is crucial for the region to continue to adapt and collaborate with international partners to address emerging cyber threats and challenges. 


## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules

### Section 6.2: Case Studies: Cyber Politics in Different Regions of the World

As the internet continues to play an increasingly important role in international relations, it is essential to examine how different regions of the world are approaching cyber politics. In this section, we will explore the unique challenges and approaches to cyber governance in Europe.

### Subsection 6.2b: Cyber Politics in Europe

Europe, as a diverse region with multiple countries and cultures, faces unique challenges in the realm of cyber politics. The European Union (EU) has been at the forefront of developing and implementing cyber norms and rules, with the aim of promoting a safe and secure cyberspace for its citizens.

One of the key challenges in Europe is the protection of personal data and privacy. The EU has taken a proactive approach to this issue, with the implementation of the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) in 2018. This regulation sets strict guidelines for the collection and use of personal data by companies and governments, with heavy penalties for non-compliance. The GDPR has been praised for its comprehensive approach to protecting personal data and has served as a model for other regions and countries.

Another important aspect of cyber politics in Europe is the protection of critical infrastructure. In recent years, there have been several high-profile cyber attacks targeting European countries, such as the 2017 WannaCry ransomware attack on the UK's National Health Service. In response, the EU has developed the Network and Information Security (NIS) Directive, which sets out security requirements for critical infrastructure operators and requires member states to have a national strategy for dealing with cyber threats.

In addition to these measures, the EU has also been actively involved in shaping global cyber norms and rules. The EU has been a strong advocate for a multi-stakeholder approach to cyber governance, similar to the one adopted by the United States. The EU has also been a vocal proponent of the principle of state responsibility in cyberspace, which holds states accountable for cyber attacks originating from their territory.

Overall, Europe has made significant progress in developing and implementing cyber norms and rules. However, there is still room for improvement, particularly in terms of coordination and cooperation among member states. As the threat landscape continues to evolve, it is crucial for Europe to continue adapting and strengthening its cyber policies to ensure a safe and secure cyberspace for its citizens.


## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules

### Section 6.2: Case Studies: Cyber Politics in Different Regions of the World

As the internet continues to play an increasingly important role in international relations, it is essential to examine how different regions of the world are approaching cyber politics. In this section, we will explore the unique challenges and approaches to cyber governance in Asia.

### Subsection 6.2c: Cyber Politics in Asia

Asia, with its diverse political landscape and rapidly growing technological advancements, faces unique challenges in the realm of cyber politics. The region is home to some of the world's largest and most technologically advanced countries, such as China, Japan, and South Korea, making it a prime target for cyber attacks.

One of the key challenges in Asia is the protection of personal data and privacy. With the rise of social media and e-commerce, the collection and use of personal data have become a major concern for individuals and governments alike. In response, many countries in Asia have implemented data protection laws, such as China's Cybersecurity Law and Japan's Act on the Protection of Personal Information. However, these laws vary in their scope and enforcement, leading to challenges in cross-border data protection.

Another important aspect of cyber politics in Asia is the protection of critical infrastructure. As the region becomes increasingly reliant on technology, the risk of cyber attacks on critical infrastructure, such as power grids and transportation systems, also increases. In response, countries like South Korea and Japan have established national cybersecurity strategies and invested in advanced technologies to protect their critical infrastructure.

In addition to these measures, Asia has also been actively involved in shaping global cyber norms and rules. China, for example, has been a strong advocate for a state-centric approach to cyber governance, emphasizing the role of governments in regulating cyberspace. On the other hand, Japan has been a proponent of a multi-stakeholder approach, promoting the involvement of non-state actors in cyber governance.

With the rapid growth of technology and the increasing interconnectedness of the world, cyber politics in Asia will continue to evolve and present new challenges. It is essential for countries in the region to work together and develop effective strategies to address these challenges and promote a safe and secure cyberspace for all.


# Cyberpolitics in International Relations: Theory, Methods, Policy":

## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules:

### Section: 6.3 The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules:

### Subsection: 6.3a Evolution of Cyber Norms

The evolution of cyber norms has been a crucial aspect of cyber politics in international relations. As the use of the internet and technology continues to grow, it has become increasingly important to establish norms and rules to govern the behavior of states and other actors in cyberspace.

One of the earliest and most significant developments in the evolution of cyber norms was the establishment of the United Nations Group of Governmental Experts (UN GGE) on Developments in the Field of Information and Telecommunications in the Context of International Security. This group, formed in 2004, was tasked with examining the issue of information security and making recommendations for international cooperation in this area. The UN GGE has since released several reports, including the 2015 report which established 11 voluntary norms for responsible state behavior in cyberspace.

Another important development in the evolution of cyber norms is the establishment of the Tallinn Manual. This manual, first published in 2013, provides guidance on how international law applies to cyber operations. It has been influential in shaping the understanding of the legal framework for cyber activities and has been endorsed by several states.

The evolution of cyber norms has also been influenced by the actions of states in cyberspace. For example, the Stuxnet attack on Iran's nuclear program in 2010 raised questions about the use of cyber weapons and the need for norms to govern their use. This incident sparked discussions on the need for a global cyber arms control regime and the development of norms for responsible state behavior in cyberspace.

In addition to state actions, the private sector has also played a role in shaping cyber norms. Companies like Microsoft and Google have advocated for the protection of user privacy and the need for transparency in government surveillance. This has led to the development of norms around data protection and privacy in cyberspace.

Overall, the evolution of cyber norms has been a dynamic and ongoing process. As technology continues to advance and new cyber threats emerge, it is essential for states and other actors to continue to adapt and develop norms to ensure responsible behavior in cyberspace.

## Chapter 6: The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules:

### Section: 6.3 The Evolution of Cyber Norms and Rules:

### Subsection: 6.3b Evolution of Cyber Rules

The evolution of cyber norms and rules has been a complex and ongoing process, shaped by the actions of states, international organizations, and private actors. As the use of technology and the internet continues to grow, it has become increasingly important to establish rules and norms to govern behavior in cyberspace.

One of the earliest developments in the evolution of cyber rules was the establishment of the United Nations Group of Governmental Experts (UN GGE) on Developments in the Field of Information and Telecommunications in the Context of International Security. This group, formed in 2004, was tasked with examining the issue of information security and making recommendations for international cooperation in this area. The UN GGE has since released several reports, including the 2015 report which established 11 voluntary norms for responsible state behavior in cyberspace.

Another important development in the evolution of cyber rules is the establishment of the Tallinn Manual. This manual, first published in 2013, provides guidance on how international law applies to cyber operations. It has been influential in shaping the understanding of the legal framework for cyber activities and has been endorsed by several states.

The actions of states in cyberspace have also played a significant role in shaping cyber rules. The Stuxnet attack on Iran's nuclear program in 2010 raised questions about the use of cyber weapons and the need for rules to govern their use. This incident sparked discussions on the need for a global cyber arms control regime and the development of rules for responsible state behavior in cyberspace.

In addition to state actions, the private sector has also played a crucial role in shaping cyber rules. Companies like Microsoft and Google have advocated for stronger cybersecurity measures and have worked with governments to establish rules and norms for responsible behavior in cyberspace. For example, Microsoft's Next-Generation Secure Computing Base (NGSCB) project aimed to create a more secure computing environment through hardware and software integration, and was a significant step towards establishing rules for responsible state behavior in cyberspace.

The evolution of cyber norms and rules is an ongoing process, and it is essential for all actors to continue to work together to establish a framework for responsible behavior in cyberspace. As technology continues to advance, it is crucial to adapt and evolve these norms and rules to address new challenges and threats in the cyber realm.
